Zootopia Club Next Master Ledger
Last refreshed: 2026-04-09 13:27:04

Project Identity
- Name: Zootopia Club Next
- Workspace root: C:\zootopia-club-next
- Primary architecture guide: Guide-Files\Zootopia_Club_Next_16_2_2_Simplified_Monorepo_Guide_2026_WORKSPACE_UPDATED.md
- Old-project reference: C:\zootopia_club_ai_platform

Current Truth Snapshot
- `apps/web` is the only live application runtime today.
- `apps/api` exists as a future extraction boundary only and does not serve production traffic.
- The repo uses npm workspaces, not pnpm workspaces or Turborepo.
- `packages/ui` does not exist in the current repo even though the guide’s target structure leaves room for it.
- Root `firebase.json` now uses Firebase App Hosting as the only web deployment path and still deploys Firestore rules/indexes plus Storage rules from the repo root.
- `apps/web/app/api/**/route.ts` is the only live backend surface today; there is no separate active root `server.ts` or root `src/*` application tree.
- The actual architecture guide lives at `Guide-Files/Zootopia_Club_Next_16_2_2_Simplified_Monorepo_Guide_2026_WORKSPACE_UPDATED.md`; the repo-root copy referenced in some prompts and older notes is not present.
- The App Hosting build path now depends on `apps/web/apphosting.yaml`, `apps/web/package-lock.json`, `apps/web/next.config.ts`, and `apps/web/scripts/normalize-standalone.mjs` as stable architecture files, not one-off deployment fixes; the standalone normalizer must keep copying `@sparticuz/chromium/bin/*` into the standalone bundle so the Pro PDF lane can launch packaged Chromium on Firebase App Hosting/Cloud Run.
- `apps/web/next.config.ts` now also explicitly allowlists `127.0.0.1` in `allowedDevOrigins` so local Next.js dev assets such as `/_next/webpack-hmr` can be requested safely when the browser reaches the dev server through `127.0.0.1` instead of only `localhost`.
- The active Firebase App Hosting backend is `zootopia-club-next-backend` at `zootopia-club-next-backend--zootopia2026.us-central1.hosted.app`, and it is wired to Firebase web app `1:38079185268:web:adcd16b5e94d3d8c52ec21`; older Firebase web apps/backends still exist in the project but are not the current repo deployment target.
- `apps/web/next.config.ts` now backfills the browser `NEXT_PUBLIC_FIREBASE_*` contract from App Hosting's build-only `FIREBASE_WEBAPP_CONFIG` when explicit public env vars are absent, so the existing client auth bootstrap works on App Hosting without duplicating public Firebase config in `apps/web/apphosting.yaml`.
- The current font/runtime presentation stack uses Plus Jakarta Sans, Alexandria, Amiri, and JetBrains Mono through `apps/web/app/layout.tsx`; older IBM Plex notes remain historical change-log context only.
- Browser Firestore access and browser Storage access are intentionally deny-all.
- Same-origin App Router Route Handlers plus the Firebase Admin SDK are the real server-authoritative data path.
- `/upload` is the only tool page that renders the full `apps/web/components/upload/upload-workspace.tsx` document-intake surface.
- `/upload` now captures a stable submitted form element reference before async upload awaits so post-success cleanup cannot throw `Cannot read properties of null (reading 'reset')` after a real durable save.
- `/assessment` and `/infographic` now consume shared document continuity through page-specific selectors plus a compact shared document handoff card, not by embedding the full upload UI.
- uploaded `documents` now preserve active-link semantics per owner through `isActive` / `supersededAt`, and the Assessment page preselects the owner’s active linked document instead of making the user relink it manually every time.
- Upload normalization now runs through `apps/web/lib/server/document-markdown.ts`, which creates the truthful local markdown snapshot used by the current direct-file runtime; Datalab Convert is no longer part of the active product path or runtime capability surface.
- `/assessment` now supports server-normalized mode selection (`question_generation` or `exam_generation`) plus question-type selection and 100%-total percentage distribution inside the existing Assessment request `options` shape, and it now stores owner-scoped result metadata including `status`, `expiresAt`, `previewRoute`, `resultRoute`, and preview/export-friendly summary fields.
- Assessment generation now prefers the original linked PDF file for Gemini models when Storage still has the binary, then falls back safely to extracted text context for unsupported file/model combinations instead of redesigning the upload pipeline.
- Assessment results now have two dedicated pages, `/assessment/preview/[id]` and `/assessment/results/[id]`, plus owner-scoped result/export endpoints under `/api/assessment/results/[id]`, `/api/assessment/export/pdf/pro/[id]`, `/api/assessment/export/pdf/fast/[id]`, and the existing JSON/Markdown/DOCX routes.
- Assessment preview/result pages and the user-facing result/export APIs now resolve records through explicit owner-only repository helpers; admins no longer piggyback on the normal user artifact surfaces for cross-owner inspection.
- `GET /api/infographic/[id]` now resolves through an explicit owner-only repository helper, so the normal user infographic readback endpoint no longer doubles as an admin cross-owner observation lane.
- Assessment preview/result pages plus both PDF lanes now share a narrow file-surface composition helper that keeps the first-page-only logo/brand rail, the compact `https://linktr.ee/ebnabdallah` QR card, the Arabic-only final support-page descriptor, the light/dark circular seal asset mapping, and the light/dark file-background asset mapping explicit instead of scattering that logic across separate renderers.
- `/assessment` now uses a single-column configuration studio with Assessment-scoped custom dropdown panels, history-driven preview/result quick actions, and an optional steering prompt that can be left blank when a linked document is selected.
- `/assessment` now also shows a post-success retention reminder only after a real saved generation commit, explaining the 3-day history window plus auto-delete behavior and linking to `/history`; the reminder auto-dismisses after exactly 60 seconds and is keyed by generation id to prevent duplicate rerender spam.
- Assessment generation now uses a server-authoritative daily credit contract for normal users only: 3 successful generations per UTC day, short-lived pre-model reservations to prevent realistic duplicate-click oversubscription, an atomic durable save plus credit-consume commit after the canonical result artifact is persisted, and admin exemption that is enforced on the server instead of in client UI.
- Assessment generations now persist a canonical owner-scoped result artifact in Storage, and JSON/Markdown/DOCX/print-HTML export artifacts are now cached under owner-scoped Storage paths when generated through the server routes.
- Legacy assessment and document records no longer default a missing `ownerRole` to `"user"` during normalization or persistence. Shared repository reads/writes now resolve missing owner roles from authoritative owner context only (stored role, same-owner session role when available, or the owner's user/Auth metadata), best-effort backfill resolved legacy records, and omit unresolved `ownerRole` fields from Firestore merge writes instead of silently reclassifying ambiguous admin-owned history.
- `apps/web/lib/server/repository.ts` now also exposes `backfillLegacyOwnerRolesForOwner(ownerUid)` as the explicit owner-scoped migration helper for intentionally repairing older document/assessment histories once the server can prove the real owner role.
- The protected shell now places the Zootopia mark in the sidebar header, groups locale plus theme controls together in the sidebar utility rail, keeps the protected sidebar theme switcher intentionally limited to visible `Light` and `Dark` choices while still tolerating older `system` cookies safely, exposes `/about` and `/contact` in the shared left sidebar for both normal users and admins, mounts a floating scroll-to-top control against the real protected scroll container, keeps the Arabic attribution seal in the page scroll flow instead of a persistent footer bar, and layers in a subtle timed bubble effect through the protected background only.
- The protected header now also carries a compact donation CTA plus a real server-backed Assessment credit badge sourced from `/api/assessment/credits`; this badge remains intentionally Assessment-scoped so users do not mistake one tool's quota for a global wallet or billing balance.
- `/upload` now keeps a visible active-document continuation card with a direct Assessment CTA and a safe owner-scoped active-file removal path through `DELETE /api/uploads?documentId=...`.
- `/api/uploads/[id]` now provides an owner-validated server download path for uploaded source files so History and other protected surfaces can retrieve the original binary without exposing Storage directly.
- Infographic is now intentionally UI-locked for non-admin users across protected nav and tool entry cards; admins retain the real Infographic studio, while non-admin users see a polished coming-soon surface on `/infographic`.
- Public informational routes now exist at `/about`, `/contact`, `/donation`, and `/hall-of-honor`, and they share a dedicated public-site layout instead of borrowing the protected workspace shell or the login-page composition.
- The new `/hall-of-honor` tribute page is intentionally hierarchical by design (Elmahdy as the primary featured hero, Adham as a respectful secondary honoree), and discovery is wired through both public/protected navigation plus a dedicated protected-home entry card.
- `/donation` now presents trust-first bilingual support messaging that explicitly covers recurring operating costs, the 2022/2023 legacy angle, continuity risk if monthly costs are not covered, and direct personal WhatsApp contact at `+201124511183`.
- `/api/contact` now provides a small server-only public contact relay that sends through Gmail SMTP runtime env vars, keeps `CONTACT_FORM_TO` off the client, and applies a silent honeypot guard instead of broad anti-spam infrastructure.
- Assessment preview/result pages, Markdown/DOCX exports, and the print/PDF export surface now share their file-facing Arabic footer through `apps/web/lib/assessment-file-branding.ts`, using the exact export line `تمت برمجة وتطوير وتمويل هذه المنصة بكل شغف وإبداع على يد ابن عبدالله يوسف، دفعة 2022، قسم كيمياء حيوان 💻❤️` without rewriting the broader protected-shell attribution source.
- Assessment preview/result/export surfaces now use a shared display parser that can split both multiline and inline MCQ options out of the saved `question` string, keep answer choices beneath the stem, prefer a compact 2x2 layout for four-choice sets when width allows, resolve marker-only answers into human-readable labels like `B) Ecosystem`, and annotate correct choices once so preview/result/PDF cards can share the same premium highlight treatment without rewriting the persisted assessment record.
- The shared Assessment pipeline now supports mixed question-type composition (MCQ, True/False, Essay, Fill blanks, Short answer, Matching, Multiple response) with per-question difficulty metadata, content-language direction derivation, and type-aware rendering across detached preview/result plus print/PDF/DOCX/Markdown/text export surfaces.
- Detached preview/result pages plus both PDF export lanes now carry the active light/dark file theme through explicit `?theme=` query params, but the assessment-specific default file mode is now `light` unless the user explicitly switches it.
- The Pro PDF lane now launches a local Chrome/Edge executable first during integrated development and only falls back to packaged `@sparticuz/chromium` on Linux server runtimes, which preserves local developer reliability on Windows/macOS while keeping Firebase App Hosting compatible.
- `apps/web/components/assessment/assessment-export-actions.tsx` now exposes distinct Pro and Fast PDF controls, with the Pro Puppeteer/Chromium lane rendered as the first hero CTA on preview pages and the Fast browser-print lane rendered immediately beside it as a clearly secondary path.
- `apps/web/app/globals.css` now adds a guarded Assessment export-toolbar spacing contract that keeps lane badges readable and avoids label crowding by combining larger badge-safe trailing padding with a 640-860px single-column layout fallback; this remains CSS-only so export route ownership and action logic stay unchanged.
- `apps/web/components/assessment/assessment-preview-shell.tsx` now owns the detached file-surface summary card used by both preview and result pages, and that shared top summary block keeps a literal `SUMMARY` badge plus theme-aware premium styling so the on-screen file header stays aligned with the Pro PDF cover treatment.
- The Pro Assessment PDF lane now lives at `/api/assessment/export/pdf/pro/[id]`, owns the Puppeteer/Chromium download flow, keeps its own `export-pdf` artifact identity plus Pro-specific version tag, and reuses the shared file-surface HTML only as a narrow rendering foundation so future premium charts/graphs/layouts can evolve independently.
- The Fast Assessment PDF lane now lives at `/api/assessment/export/pdf/fast/[id]`, owns the lightweight same-origin browser-print HTML flow, keeps its own `export-print-html` artifact identity plus Fast-specific version tag, and remains the speed-first fallback/quick-export path instead of hiding behind a mixed `surface=print` branch.
- The shared Assessment export pagination contract now counts structured question-detail blocks when deciding page fallback, keeps each print page body separate from its footer row, and keeps the support/signature/footer sheet as one final owned page so the footer cannot spill into a ghost page while Pro/Fast lane separation stays intact.
- `GET /api/assessment/export/pdf/[id]` is now compatibility-only and immediately redirects older links to the explicit Pro or Fast lane route, so the real generation logic no longer lives behind one confusing mixed contract.
- `/history` now exists as a dedicated owner-scoped protected route that aggregates retained uploads plus generated assessments/exports from the existing repository layer instead of inventing a second backend.
- Assessment and document retention now share one 3-day lifecycle contract with lazy cleanup: expired uploads, assessment records, canonical result files, and persisted export artifacts are removed on server read/list access instead of only being hidden in UI state.
- `POST /api/internal/maintenance/expired-uploads` now validates the bearer secret with a timing-safe comparison, reducing token-probing signal leakage while preserving the existing secret-gated scheduler contract.
- Regular user login and admin login are intentionally separate.
- Both auth bootstrap edges (`/api/auth/bootstrap` and `/api/auth/admin/bootstrap`) are now server-throttled with route-scoped limits, while preserving independent regular-user versus admin sign-in contracts.
- Admin authority is claims-first: allowlisted email plus Firebase custom claim `admin: true`.
- Session and route isolation remain request-bound on the server: `verifySessionCookie(..., true)` revalidates the session cookie on every request, admin routes and APIs still resolve through explicit admin-session helpers, and owner-facing assessment/export/history reads remain bound to `ownerUid` instead of shared mutable session state.
- The admin dashboard now includes a server-rendered recent platform activity feed sourced from `adminActivityLogs`, and the app now records login/session, upload, assessment, export, download, and cleanup activity there for admin-safe observability.
- `/admin` and `/admin/users` now merge the full Firebase Auth account inventory with stored Firestore user metadata, so admin user visibility is no longer capped at 100 hydrated user documents or limited only to accounts that already completed a normal bootstrap flow.
- `/admin/users` now uses compact per-user entry cards with inline expansion panels for role/status/access/credit management, replacing the previous cramped right-rail table-actions pattern while preserving the same admin-only APIs and server authority.
- Admin block/unblock now updates both the persistent `users.status` field and Firebase Auth's `disabled` flag, then revokes refresh tokens so suspension is enforced by backend/session authority even against already-issued sessions.
- Mandatory non-admin profile completion is enforced server-side before access to the main user workspace and now requires full name, university code, verified phone number, and nationality, while admins remain exempt. `/settings` now renders Profile Completion as the dominant full-width workflow surface, keeps Runtime Status directly below it, moves the signed-in account summary into a compact secondary rail, uses a real Egypt-default international phone input plus searchable country selectors for phone/nationality, persists verified phone metadata (`phoneNumber`, `phoneVerifiedAt`, `phoneCountryIso2`, `phoneCountryCallingCode`) server-authoritatively, and still routes phone verification only through Firebase Web Auth (`RecaptchaVerifier` + `signInWithPhoneNumber`) into the self-only `POST /api/users/me/phone-verification` handoff, which is now locally rate-limited.
- Root `.env.local` is the canonical local environment source; repo-root `.env`, `cloudrun.env`, `netlify.toml`, `Dockerfile`, `cloudbuild.yaml`, `deployment/runtime-manifest.json`, and `tests/*` are not active current-repo paths.

Guide Alignment Notes
- The guide remains the main architectural reference.
- The repo intentionally differs from the guide in a few current-state areas:
  - `apps/api` is present but deferred.
  - npm workspaces are used instead of pnpm or Turborepo.
  - `packages/ui` is not currently present.
  - The repo now aligns with the official Firebase recommendation by using App Hosting as the active deployment path for the Next.js app.

Current Repo Reality Versus Older Audit Checklists
- The current repo does not contain root `server.ts`, root `server/*`, root `src/App.tsx`, root `src/auth/*`, root `src/ai/*`, root `src/features/*`, root `src/components/*`, root `src/services/*`, or root `src/routing/*`.
- The current repo also does not contain active root `netlify.toml`, `Dockerfile`, `cloudbuild.yaml`, `cloudrun.env`, `deployment/runtime-manifest.json`, repo-root `.env`, or `tests/*`.
- Historical or reference-only deployment material survives under `docs/legacy-reference/*` and `Guide-Files/*`, including `docs/legacy-reference/cloudrun.reference.env`, but those files do not define the active runtime path.
- Future agents should treat workspace-based paths under `apps/web`, `apps/api`, `packages/shared-*`, `firebase`, `docs`, and `Guide-Files` as the current source tree, and should not assume that older single-app root paths still exist.

Monorepo Structure
- Root ownership
  - `package.json`: workspace orchestration and root scripts
  - `package-lock.json`: canonical lockfile
  - `tsconfig.base.json`, `tsconfig.json`: shared TypeScript baseline
  - `eslint.config.mjs`: root lint config
  - `.env.example`: current environment contract
  - `firebase.json`, `.firebaserc`: Firebase deployment wiring
  - `README.md`, `docs/`, `Guide-Files/`: repo docs and reference material
- `apps/web`
  - `app/`: App Router pages, layouts, and Route Handlers
  - `components/`: UI and client-side interaction components
  - `components/ui/`: shared button/input/background primitives and local design-system utilities
  - `lib/`: request context, preferences, auth helpers, server modules, AI orchestration, Firebase integration
  - `messages/`: EN/AR message catalogs
  - `public/`: static assets
  - `proxy.ts`: optimistic request-time redirects only
- `apps/api`
  - Placeholder workspace package for future backend extraction
  - Current source files only describe its deferred role
- `packages/shared-config`
  - App identity, Firebase project/database constants, route constants, env cookie keys, feature flags, AI model catalog
- `packages/shared-types`
  - Shared auth, user, API, document, assessment, infographic, and admin contracts
- `packages/shared-utils`
  - Validation, upload policy, RTL helpers, date helpers, and small pure utilities
- `firebase`
  - `firestore.rules`
  - `firestore.indexes.json`
  - `storage.rules`
- `scripts/firebase`
  - Firebase env bootstrap and admin maintenance scripts
- `docs`
  - Active architecture notes plus legacy-reference material for migration context only

Dependency And Runtime Baseline
- Root workspace baseline
  - Node engine: `>=20.9.0`
  - npm workspaces across `apps/*` and `packages/*`
  - TypeScript `^5`
  - ESLint `^9`
  - Tailwind CSS `^4`
- `apps/web` application baseline
  - Next.js `16.2.2`
  - React `19.2.4`
  - React DOM `19.2.4`
  - Firebase Web SDK `^12.11.0`
  - Firebase Admin SDK `^13.5.0`
  - DOCX export layer: `docx` `^9.5.1`
  - QR generation for branded file surfaces: `qrcode` `^1.5.4`
  - UI utility layer: `@radix-ui/react-slot`, `class-variance-authority`, `clsx`, `tailwind-merge`
  - motion layer: `framer-motion` `12.38.0` plus package-level `motion` `^12.38.0`
  - icon layer: `lucide-react` `1.7.0`
- Build/deploy baseline
  - `apps/web` builds with standalone output enabled
  - App Hosting depends on the app-local lockfile in `apps/web/package-lock.json`
  - `apps/web/package.json` runs `postbuild` through `apps/web/scripts/normalize-standalone.mjs` so Firebase App Hosting sees the bundle structure it expects

Current Visual Identity And UI System
- `apps/web/app/globals.css` now defines the current emerald-and-gold premium scientific visual system, including glass surfaces, hover states, motion tokens, auth-state styling, and shared background/elevation utilities for both light and dark themes.
- `apps/web/app/layout.tsx` now mounts `apps/web/components/ui/vital-background.tsx`, which provides the animated global glow/noise background layer behind the entire app shell.
- The current font stack is loaded through `next/font` using Plus Jakarta Sans, Alexandria, Amiri, and JetBrains Mono.
- `apps/web/app/(protected)/layout.tsx` now mounts `apps/web/components/layout/protected-workspace-background.tsx`, which keeps `apps/web/public/my-app-background.png` scoped to protected routes only and layers subtle dimming, animated grid/orb/beam ambience, texture, and a lightweight timed bubble pass without touching public auth backgrounds.
- `apps/web/components/layout/protected-shell.tsx` and `apps/web/components/layout/shell-nav.tsx` now anchor the protected-shell toolbar/sidebar contract: logo in the sidebar header, locale plus theme controls grouped in the sidebar utilities, a floating scroll-to-top button, and a compact branded Arabic attribution seal that lives at the end of the protected scroll flow instead of in a persistent footer bar.
- `apps/web/components/site/public-site-shell.tsx` now defines the shared premium public-info header/footer surface for `/about`, `/contact`, `/donation`, and `/hall-of-honor`, keeping those routes visually cohesive without leaking protected-shell ownership into public pages.
- `apps/web/components/assessment/assessment-studio.tsx` now uses `apps/web/components/assessment/assessment-field-select.tsx` for Assessment-only dropdown panels and an emerald/cyan/gold studio surface that aligns with the protected shell instead of the older violet-heavy two-column layout.
- `apps/web/components/layout/protected-signature-seal.tsx` plus `apps/web/lib/branding/protected-signature.ts` now define the shared attribution seal reused by the protected footer, Assessment preview/result surfaces, and export renderers.
- `apps/web/lib/assessment-file-branding.ts` now defines the dedicated file-surface background/logo/footer/QR metadata used by detached Assessment preview/result pages and the print/PDF export surface, including the first-page-only premium framing rules future agents should keep aligned.
- `apps/web/lib/site-content.ts` now holds the bilingual long-form public-site copy, including the structured Donation-page cost/continuity/WhatsApp messaging, plus the compact donation/balance labels used by the protected header, which keeps those informational strings out of the core workspace message catalog.
- A local shared UI primitive layer now exists in `apps/web/components/ui/button.tsx`, `apps/web/components/ui/input.tsx`, and `apps/web/lib/utils.ts`.
- The current UX direction is intentionally more visual and less text-heavy than earlier passes, with stronger CTA hierarchy, route-specific accent colors, and glassmorphic card treatments across Home, Upload, Assessment, Infographic, Settings, and Admin.
- `apps/web/app/(public)/admin/login/page.tsx` plus `apps/web/components/auth/admin-login-panel.tsx` now keep the admin entrance on a compact copy-light auth layout (shared media copy hidden and non-essential helper text removed) so the separate admin sign-in flow stays operational with less scrolling on mobile, tablet, laptop, desktop, and ultra-wide viewports.
- Current page-focus rule: the protected shell is shared, but each major tool page owns only its own page-scale UI. Shared document continuity appears as compact support UI only and no longer duplicates the upload page inside Assessment or Infographic.
- Older IBM Plex-era notes remain historically accurate for earlier redesign phases in the change log, but they no longer describe the current live typography stack.

Route Map
- Public routes
  - `/about`
  - `/contact`
  - `/donation`
  - `/hall-of-honor`
  - `/login`
  - `/admin/login`
- Authenticated non-admin shell
  - `/settings`
- Completion-required non-admin routes
  - `/`
  - `/upload`
  - `/history`
  - `/assessment`
  - `/assessment/preview/[id]`
  - `/assessment/results/[id]`
  - `/infographic`
- Admin routes
  - `/admin`
  - `/admin/users`

Route Ownership Clarification
- `/upload`
  - owns the full upload and document-preparation surface through `apps/web/app/(protected)/(completed)/upload/page.tsx`
  - is the only route that renders `apps/web/components/upload/upload-workspace.tsx`
- `/assessment`
  - owns assessment generation, active linked-document selection, optional prompt-driven or document-driven setup, assessment history, and preview/result quick actions through `apps/web/app/(protected)/(completed)/assessment/page.tsx` and `apps/web/components/assessment/assessment-studio.tsx`
  - preview/result ownership is split cleanly across `apps/web/app/(protected)/(completed)/assessment/preview/[id]/page.tsx`, `apps/web/app/(protected)/(completed)/assessment/results/[id]/page.tsx`, and the shared viewer/export components under `apps/web/components/assessment/*`
  - does not render the full upload workspace
- `/infographic`
  - keeps the real infographic generation studio for admins through `apps/web/app/(protected)/(completed)/infographic/page.tsx` and `apps/web/components/infographic/infographic-studio.tsx`
  - renders a polished non-admin coming-soon placeholder in the same route without pretending that the placeholder is the authorization boundary
  - does not render the full upload workspace
- `/about`, `/contact`, `/donation`, and `/hall-of-honor`
  - share public informational layout ownership through `apps/web/app/(site)/layout.tsx` and `apps/web/components/site/public-site-shell.tsx`
  - do not borrow protected-shell layout ownership and do not expose the private contact destination email in their client-visible UI
- Protected shell
  - shared layout only through `apps/web/app/(protected)/layout.tsx`, `apps/web/components/layout/protected-shell.tsx`, and `apps/web/components/layout/shell-nav.tsx`
  - does not decide tool-page content ownership

Shared State Versus Shared Page UI
- Shared document state remains intentional and server-loaded through `listDocumentsForUser(...)` on the route page, then passed into tool studios as `initialDocuments`.
- Shared linked-document continuity remains intentional through `documentId`, owner-scoped repository lookups, and compact page-specific UI.
- Shared page-scale UI is intentionally constrained: only `/upload` renders `apps/web/components/upload/upload-workspace.tsx`.
- `apps/web/components/document/document-context-card.tsx` is a compact shared support component, not a second upload page.

Backend Runtime And Service Ownership
- The active backend is the Next App Router server surface inside `apps/web/app/api`, not `apps/api`.
- All live route handlers are pinned to the Node runtime because they rely on cookies, Firebase Admin, Firestore, Storage, and multipart uploads.
- Server-only responsibility split
  - `apps/web/app/api/**/route.ts`: request parsing, auth gating, response shaping
  - `apps/web/lib/server/session.ts`: session verification and route/API guards
  - `apps/web/lib/server/repository.ts`: Firestore-backed persistence with a local in-memory fallback when Firebase Admin runtime is unavailable, including active-document normalization plus assessment result lifecycle normalization
  - `apps/web/lib/server/document-runtime.ts`: upload validation, direct-file markdown snapshot orchestration, Storage persistence attempts, and linked-binary reloads for direct-file Assessment generation
  - `apps/web/lib/server/document-markdown.ts`: current local document snapshot helper for upload normalization and text-context fallback continuity
  - `apps/web/lib/server/assessment-linked-document.ts`: Assessment-only linked-document resolution that prefers direct PDF input when the selected provider supports it
  - `apps/web/lib/server/assessment-file-qr.ts`: server-side QR data URL generation for the branded Assessment file surfaces
  - `apps/web/lib/server/contact-mail.ts`: server-only Gmail SMTP relay for the public Contact page that reads runtime env vars in local dev and Firebase App Hosting without exposing the admin destination or credentials to the client
  - `apps/web/lib/server/assessment-retention.ts`: 3-day Assessment expiry window and route/lifecycle helpers
  - `apps/web/lib/server/assessment-preview.ts`: normalized bilingual Assessment preview/result model generation
  - `apps/web/lib/server/assessment-exporter.ts`: JSON, Markdown, and DOCX artifact generation from one normalized preview model
  - `apps/web/lib/server/assessment-print-renderer.ts`: print-first HTML export surface used by the lightweight PDF route
  - `apps/web/lib/server/runtime.ts`: runtime capability flags returned by inspection endpoints
  - `apps/web/lib/server/firebase-admin.ts`: managed-credentials or service-account Admin bootstrap
- `apps/api` remains a deliberate future extraction boundary only
  - `apps/api/src/app.ts` describes the package as `future-extraction-target`
  - `apps/api/src/server.ts` explicitly says Phase 1 runtime is owned by `apps/web` route handlers

Auth And Session Architecture
- Session model
  - One secure httpOnly session cookie: `zc_session`
  - Preference cookies: `zc_theme`, `zc_locale`
  - Cookie names are defined in `packages/shared-config/src/env.ts`
- User login flow
  - Public entry point: `/login`
  - Firebase Web SDK Google sign-in happens client-side
  - Client auth persistence is intentionally in-memory only during bootstrap
  - `POST /api/auth/bootstrap` verifies the Google ID token server-side, creates the session cookie, mirrors/upserts the user document, and returns the correct redirect target
  - Client signs out its Firebase Web state after bootstrap so the session cookie remains the authoritative long-lived session
- Admin login flow
  - Public entry point: `/admin/login`
  - Separate UI and separate bootstrap path
  - Admin identifier resolution happens server-side first
  - Real credential step is Firebase Email/Password
  - `POST /api/auth/admin/bootstrap` verifies recent sign-in, provider `password`, allowlisted email, and `admin: true` claim before issuing the same session cookie type
- Route protection
  - `apps/web/proxy.ts` only checks cookie presence and redirects unauthenticated requests optimistically
  - Real authorization stays in server code through:
    - `getSessionSnapshot()`
    - `requireAuthenticatedUser()`
    - `requireCompletedUser()`
    - `requireAdminUser()`
- Session user source of truth
  - `apps/web/lib/server/session.ts` verifies the session cookie through Firebase Admin Auth
  - The decoded token is combined with the Firestore user record through `upsertUserFromAuth()`
  - Active/suspended state comes from the Firestore mirror

Admin Login Architecture
- Only these emails may hold admin authority:
  - `alahlyeagle@gmail.com`
  - `elmahdy@admin.com`
  - `alahlyeagle13@gmail.com`
- Supported admin usernames:
  - `elmahdy`
  - `alahlyeagle`
- Admin authority rule
  - allowlisted email
  - plus Firebase custom claim `admin === true`
- Firestore `role` and `status` remain mirrored for UI/admin management, but they are not sufficient by themselves for privileged access
- Key files
  - `apps/web/lib/server/admin-auth.ts`
  - `apps/web/app/api/auth/admin/resolve-identifier/route.ts`
  - `apps/web/app/api/auth/admin/bootstrap/route.ts`
  - `scripts/firebase/set-admin-claims.mjs`
  - `scripts/firebase/set-admin-passwords.mjs`

Mandatory Profile Completion Architecture
- Applies to authenticated non-admin users only
- Required fields
  - `fullName`
  - `universityCode`
  - `phoneNumber`
  - `phoneVerifiedAt`
  - `nationality`
  - `profileCompleted`
  - `profileCompletedAt`
- Validation rules
  - `fullName`
    - trim and normalize repeated whitespace
    - normalized length 12 through 120 characters
    - at least 4 meaningful parts
    - Arabic and/or English letters only, with internal apostrophes or hyphens allowed
    - each part must contain at least 2 letters after stripping apostrophes and hyphens
  - `universityCode`
    - exactly 7 digits
    - first 2 digits must be a cohort prefix from `13` through `31`
    - prefixes map to years `2013` through `2031`
  - `phoneNumber`
    - server-verified through Firebase phone OTP token handoff only
    - normalized as E.164 (`+<countrycode><number>`)
  - `phoneVerifiedAt`
    - must exist alongside a valid E.164 phone number for non-admin completion
  - `nationality`
    - trim and normalize whitespace
    - normalized length 2 through 80 characters
    - Arabic/English letters with spaces, apostrophes, periods, or hyphens only
- Persistence model
  - stored on `users/{uid}`
  - server recomputes `profileCompleted` from stored fields instead of trusting client input
  - phone verification persistence is server-authoritative through `POST /api/users/me/phone-verification`
- Enforcement points
  - bootstrap redirect shaping in `POST /api/auth/bootstrap`
  - session helper checks in `apps/web/lib/server/session.ts`
  - completion-only protected pages under `apps/web/app/(protected)/(completed)`
  - protected user APIs return `PROFILE_INCOMPLETE` if the user is still gated
- Settings save flow
  - `PATCH /api/users/me/profile` is the only self-service save path for stored profile fields in Settings
  - `POST /api/users/me/phone-verification` is the only self-service path that can mark phone verification as complete
  - `apps/web/components/settings/profile-settings-form.tsx` provides the client UI for both normal users and admins
- Admin policy
  - admins are exempt from the non-admin completion gate
  - admins still stay inside the same self-only ownership boundary in Settings; this route does not allow cross-account editing

Firebase Integration
- Firebase project: `zootopia2026`
- Firestore database: `zootopia-club-next-database`
- Default storage bucket: `zootopia2026.firebasestorage.app` unless overridden
- Live Firestore collections used by the application
  - `users`
  - `documents`
  - `assessmentGenerations`
  - `infographicGenerations`
  - `adminActivityLogs`
- Live Storage path pattern
  - `documents/{ownerUid}/{documentId}/{fileName}`
- Firebase Admin bootstrap
  - `apps/web/lib/server/firebase-admin.ts`
  - supports canonical `FIREBASE_*` env names and older `FIREBASE_ADMIN_*` aliases
  - binds Firestore explicitly to the named database `zootopia-club-next-database`
- Firebase client bootstrap
  - `apps/web/lib/firebase/client.ts`
  - uses the modular Firebase Web SDK from `firebase/app` and `firebase/auth`
  - requires the full public web contract:
    - `NEXT_PUBLIC_FIREBASE_API_KEY`
    - `NEXT_PUBLIC_FIREBASE_AUTH_DOMAIN`
    - `NEXT_PUBLIC_FIREBASE_PROJECT_ID`
    - `NEXT_PUBLIC_FIREBASE_STORAGE_BUCKET`
    - `NEXT_PUBLIC_FIREBASE_MESSAGING_SENDER_ID`
    - `NEXT_PUBLIC_FIREBASE_APP_ID`
  - on Firebase App Hosting, `apps/web/next.config.ts` now mirrors the backend-linked build-only `FIREBASE_WEBAPP_CONFIG` into those six public env keys before Next compiles the client bundle
  - keeps client auth persistence in-memory only during login bootstrap

AI, Model, And Provider Orchestration
- Model catalog authority
  - `packages/shared-config/src/models.ts` defines the supported model ids, provider families, display labels, env keys, and tool scopes
  - `apps/web/lib/ai/models.ts` re-exports the shared model catalog into the web runtime
- Provider/runtime resolution
  - `apps/web/lib/server/ai/provider-runtime.ts` maps model ids to provider-specific env names and reports whether Google or Qwen-style runtime credentials are configured
  - `apps/web/lib/server/runtime.ts` exposes provider and Firebase readiness through runtime flags
- Prompt/build flow
  - `apps/web/lib/server/ai/prompt-orchestrator.ts` assembles prompt context for assessment and infographic generation, including the current assessment rule that tasteful educational emojis may be used sparingly and must remain preserved directly inside JSON output strings
  - `apps/web/app/api/assessment/route.ts` and `apps/web/app/api/infographic/route.ts` attach optional document context from stored document markdown before generation
- Current generation reality
  - assessment generation is now provider-aware and server-side only:
    - Google Gemini assessment models run through the Google runtime path
    - `qwen3.5-flash` runs through the Alibaba DashScope OpenAI-compatible runtime and must use the US (Virginia) endpoint
  - infographic generation still returns SVG fallback output while external provider-backed infographic execution remains deferred
  - uploaded document context now comes from the local direct-file snapshot helper in `apps/web/lib/server/document-markdown.ts`, with original-file reuse preferred where the current server/runtime supports it

Firestore, Storage, Rules, And Indexes Strategy
- Firestore Rules
  - File: `firebase/firestore.rules`
  - Current strategy: deny all browser/client SDK access
  - The live app uses Route Handlers plus Firebase Admin SDK for all real reads and writes
  - Rules comments were refreshed on 2026-04-01 to document:
    - named-database deployment through `firebase.json`
    - Admin SDK bypass behavior
    - server-side enforcement of auth/admin/profile-completion rules
  - Rule logic was not changed during the 2026-04-01 audit
- Firestore Indexes
  - File: `firebase/firestore.indexes.json`
  - Current composite indexes support owner/date list queries for:
    - `documents`
    - `assessmentGenerations`
    - `infographicGenerations`
  - No profile-completion-specific index is required because that flow uses direct document lookups/writes on `users/{uid}`
- Storage Rules
  - File: `firebase/storage.rules`
  - Current strategy: deny all browser/client SDK access
  - Comments document the live server-managed document binary path
- Security model
  - Firestore Rules and Storage Rules protect browser access only
  - Firebase Admin SDK bypasses both by design
  - The real trust boundary is server code, not client-side Firebase access

  - `NEXT_PUBLIC_FIREBASE_API_KEY`
  - `NEXT_PUBLIC_FIREBASE_AUTH_DOMAIN`
  - `NEXT_PUBLIC_FIREBASE_PROJECT_ID`
  - `NEXT_PUBLIC_FIREBASE_STORAGE_BUCKET`

  - `SMTP_PASS`

  - `CONTACT_FORM_TO`

  - `DASHSCOPE_API_KEY`
  - optional model-selection env vars referenced from `packages/shared-config/src/models.ts`
- Important env notes
  - `.env.example` is the canonical repo env contract
  - root `.env.local` is the canonical local env file for both root Firebase scripts and `apps/web`
  - `apps/web/next.config.ts` reloads the root env through `@next/env` so the live Next.js app sees the same Firebase settings as the workspace scripts
  - `.env.example` currently includes project-specific public Firebase identifiers while keeping server-only credentials blank; it is a real contract file, not a generic neutral placeholder
  - `.env.example` now matches the active App Hosting backend-linked Firebase web app id `1:38079185268:web:adcd16b5e94d3d8c52ec21`
  - `.env.example` now carries the server-only Gmail SMTP contact-form contract (`SMTP_HOST`, `SMTP_PORT`, `SMTP_SECURE`, `SMTP_USER`, `SMTP_PASS`, `EMAIL_FROM`, `CONTACT_FORM_TO`) for the public Contact page relay and no longer advertises retired Datalab env settings
  - repo-root `.env` is not part of the verified current repo
  - `cloudrun.env` is not part of the verified current repo; only `docs/legacy-reference/cloudrun.reference.env` survives as historical reference
  - `serviceAccountKeyNext.json` is local bootstrap material only and is not a runtime source of truth
  - `apps/web` does not rely on a separate app-local `.env.local`; the root `.env.local` is the intended shared local source
  - App Hosting user env vars are now code-managed in `apps/web/apphosting.yaml` for the active backend, including BUILD-scoped browser-safe Firebase config and RUNTIME non-secret server config; the same file now references Cloud Secret Manager secret names for sensitive values, while real secret values remain external to source control and `FIREBASE_WEBAPP_CONFIG` backfill in `apps/web/next.config.ts` remains a safety-net path when explicit `NEXT_PUBLIC_FIREBASE_*` values are absent
  - The owner-requested shared admin password must never be stored in `.env` files, Firestore, Storage rules, Storage metadata, client code, or public config

Deployment Strategy
- Current repo deployment wiring
  - `firebase.json` deploys App Hosting from `./apps/web`
  - `firebase.json` also deploys Firestore rules and indexes to `zootopia-club-next-database`
  - `firebase.json` keeps Storage rules deployment at the root Firebase layer
- Local integrated development
  - Frontend: `apps/web`
  - Backend: same-origin Route Handlers in `apps/web/app/api/**/route.ts`
  - Path behavior: browser code uses relative `/api/*` requests against the same dev origin
  - Auth/session behavior: host-scoped `zc_session` cookie, optimistic proxy redirects, and server-side session verification
  - Env assumptions: root `.env.local` is loaded into `apps/web` through `@next/env`
  - Local resilience note: when Firebase Admin runtime is unavailable, the repository layer can fall back to an in-memory store for development continuity; this is not a production source of truth
- Firebase App Hosting
  - Status: active and only canonical web deployment target
  - Active backend verified on 2026-04-03: `zootopia-club-next-backend` at `zootopia-club-next-backend--zootopia2026.us-central1.hosted.app`
  - Frontend: Next.js pages, layouts, static assets, and public auth surfaces from `apps/web`
  - Backend: the same App Router Route Handlers under `apps/web/app/api/**/route.ts`, deployed in the App Hosting runtime
  - Path behavior: same-origin frontend and backend; client code continues to use relative `/api/*` calls with `credentials: "same-origin"`
  - Auth/session behavior: the same host-scoped session cookie and server-authoritative redirect logic as local development
  - Firebase Auth authorized domains currently include `zootopia-club-next-backend--zootopia2026.us-central1.hosted.app`
  - Env/deployment assumptions: root `firebase.json`, app-local `apps/web/apphosting.yaml`, app-local `apps/web/package-lock.json`, standalone output from `apps/web/next.config.ts`, and bundle normalization in `apps/web/scripts/normalize-standalone.mjs`
  - Root npm scripts expose `firebase:deploy` and `firebase:app:deploy` as the canonical deploy commands
- Firebase Hosting + Cloud Run
  - Status: historical/reference only
  - Frontend/backend split: not actively wired in the current repo
  - Path behavior: reference material only under `docs/legacy-reference/*`
  - Auth/session behavior: not an active current deployment contract and should not be treated as one
  - Relevant files: `docs/legacy-reference/firebase.hosting-cloud-run.reference.json`, `docs/legacy-reference/cloudrun.reference.env`, and related legacy-reference docs
- Netlify frontend + Cloud Run backend
  - Status: conceptual future option only, not a verified active path
  - Frontend/backend split: would be cross-origin by default unless a separate proxy/rewrite layer were introduced
  - Path behavior: the current client runtime is not wired for a checked-in cross-origin backend because it assumes relative same-origin `/api/*` requests
  - Auth/session behavior: the current session-cookie model is same-origin oriented, so this path would require additional deployment-specific integration work
  - Current repo evidence: there is no active `netlify.toml`, `Dockerfile`, `cloudbuild.yaml`, `cloudrun.env`, or `deployment/runtime-manifest.json`
- Other backend-capable paths
  - No other active backend-capable deployment path is checked into this repo today
  - `apps/api` remains a future extraction boundary only and should not be mistaken for a deployed backend service

  - `apps/api` traffic is intentionally disabled

Important Security Assumptions And Trust Boundaries
- Firebase Admin SDK bypasses Firestore Rules and Storage Rules by design
- Browser clients do not read or write Firestore or Storage directly in the current architecture
- `proxy.ts` is never the final authorization layer
- Admin authority requires both allowlisted identity and Firebase custom claim `admin: true`
- Firestore `role` and `status` are mirrors for UX and admin operations, not the sole authority for privileged access
- Profile completion is enforced server-side and cannot be unlocked by UI state alone
- The session cookie is the authoritative long-lived session
- Firebase Web SDK auth state is cleared after session bootstrap
- Server credentials and provider keys must remain outside the client graph
- The shared admin password model is weak and should eventually be replaced with unique credentials plus MFA

Current Behavior And Boundaries
- Anonymous user
  - can access `/login` and `/admin/login`
  - is redirected away from protected routes by proxy and/or server guards
- Authenticated non-admin with incomplete profile
  - can hold a valid session cookie
  - is redirected to `/settings`
  - cannot access `/`, `/assessment`, `/infographic`, or protected user APIs until completion is saved and re-read
- Authenticated non-admin with completed profile
  - can access the full user workspace
  - lands on `/upload` after successful login or profile completion
  - keeps `/` as the protected overview route rather than the primary upload landing
  - can use uploads and assessment generation
  - sees Infographic as a coming-soon UI-locked surface in protected navigation/cards and on `/infographic`
- Authenticated admin
  - must use the separate admin login flow
  - is protected by claims-first server checks
  - is exempt from the non-admin profile-completion gate
  - lands in `/admin`, not `/upload`, after successful admin login
  - retains infographic studio access in the protected user workspace
- Suspended user
  - cannot start or continue a valid session regardless of route intent

Generated Artifacts And Non-Source-Of-Truth Paths
- Generated build artifacts are not architectural source of truth:
  - `.next`
  - `apps/web/.next`
  - `*.tsbuildinfo`
  - `.tmp-dev-stdout.txt`
  - `.tmp-dev-stderr.txt`
  - `debug.log`
- Local scratch/reference files are also not runtime source of truth:
  - `apps/code-backup.txt`
- These files may exist locally after builds or verification runs and should not be used to infer runtime architecture

- 2026-04-09 12:46:30 | Settings OTP Root-Cause Fix: Dedicated reCAPTCHA Zone + Deterministic Send Gate
  - Mandatory-first-step compliance:
    - reread `zootopia-club-next-ledger.txt` fully before implementation.
    - launched `Explore` subagent first for read-only diagnosis.
    - completed direct full-file reads before edits for:
      - `apps/web/components/settings/profile-settings-form.tsx`
      - `apps/web/app/globals.css`
      - `apps/web/lib/firebase/client.ts`
      - `apps/web/app/api/users/me/phone-verification/route.ts`
      - `apps/web/messages/en.json`
      - `apps/web/messages/ar.json`
    - checked local Next.js App Router docs before editing:
      - `node_modules/next/dist/docs/01-app/index.md`
  - Exact root cause confirmed in this pass:
    - send-OTP could stall before `accounts:sendVerificationCode` because the reCAPTCHA token challenge was unresolved while the UI already moved into a loading state.
    - previous invisible verifier rendering allowed Google challenge UI/badge to appear in awkward floating positions, overlapping unrelated Settings controls.
    - this made the flow look broken and could fall back to generic unavailability messaging after recaptcha expiration/failure paths.
  - Surgical fix applied:
    - `apps/web/components/settings/profile-settings-form.tsx`
      - replaced invisible verifier behavior with a dedicated in-panel reCAPTCHA mount (`size: "normal"`) scoped to the Settings OTP section.
      - added explicit recaptcha readiness state (`isRecaptchaReady`) and rendering state (`isRecaptchaRendering`).
      - gated Send OTP until the challenge is solved; send no longer starts while token is unresolved.
      - added focused Firebase auth error mapping for captcha/app-credential failures to user guidance instead of collapsing into one generic message.
      - reset/reinitialize verifier after send attempts to keep retries deterministic and avoid stale token state.
      - added high-value comments documenting scope/ownership and future-agent guardrails.
    - `apps/web/app/globals.css`
      - added `settings-recaptcha-shell` and `settings-recaptcha-slot` styles (light/dark/system) to keep reCAPTCHA visually contained within OTP panel.
      - added mobile-safe overflow/scale guardrails for the embedded widget.
    - `apps/web/messages/en.json`
      - added `settingsPhoneRecaptchaPrompt`.
    - `apps/web/messages/ar.json`
      - added synchronized Arabic key `settingsPhoneRecaptchaPrompt`.
  - Authority boundaries preserved intentionally:
    - retained Firebase phone architecture (`RecaptchaVerifier` + `signInWithPhoneNumber`).
    - retained server-authoritative OTP confirmation persistence via `/api/users/me/phone-verification`.
    - no backend ownership transfer, no secret/client-authority changes, no unrelated route contract changes.
  - Files changed in this pass:

- 2026-04-07 03:05:00 | Upload Post-Success `reset` Null Error Fix
  - Root cause addressed: `apps/web/components/upload/upload-workspace.tsx` called `event.currentTarget.reset()` after async upload awaits and state updates. In that post-await phase, the synthetic event `currentTarget` can be null, which raised `Cannot read properties of null (reading 'reset')` even when `POST /api/uploads` had already succeeded.
  - Bug classification: real client runtime bug in post-success cleanup (not backend/data-loss). Backend intake/storage/runtime already completed durable success before the throw, so the active document and recent upload were correct while the UI still surfaced a false error.
  - What changed: captured a stable form element reference at submit start (`const formElement = event.currentTarget`) and reset through that stable reference (`formElement.reset()`) after successful response handling. Added a high-value comment so future agents do not reintroduce stale-event reset calls.
  - What was preserved intentionally: same `/upload` page ownership, same `POST /api/uploads` same-origin server path, same `createDocumentRecord(...)` + `saveDocument(...)` durable sequence, same active-document continuation card, same Assessment CTA continuity, same active-file removal flow, and same App Hosting compatibility/runtime boundaries.
  - Changed files:

- 2026-04-02 | Admin Claim Refresh Hardening, Global Pointer Contract, And Upload-First Landing Route
  - What was done: Centralized the default allowlisted admin identities in shared config, updated the admin runtime gate to distinguish a truly missing `admin: true` claim from a stale post-claim token, reordered repository role writes so Firebase custom claims remain the primary source of truth, added a one-time fresh-token retry in the admin login client flow, and upgraded the admin login guidance/status copy to explain the actual recovery path.
  - Firebase verification and admin-flow clarification: `npm run firebase:admin:set-claims -- --dry-run` was executed successfully on 2026-04-02 against the configured Firebase project and confirmed that `alahlyeagle@gmail.com`, `elmahdy@admin.com`, and `alahlyeagle13@gmail.com` already exist in Firebase Auth and already have admin claims. That means the reported admin-login failure was not caused by missing claim assignment on those accounts; it was consistent with stale token/session state after claim activation. The hardening now surfaces that distinction explicitly.
  - Owner runbook after `npm run firebase:admin:set-claims`: 1. Make sure the intended admin account already exists in Firebase Auth. 2. Run `npm run firebase:admin:set-claims -- --dry-run` first to verify the exact target accounts. 3. If claims are missing, rerun without `--dry-run`. 4. After the command completes, each admin must sign out, wait a few seconds for token refresh propagation, and sign back in through `/admin/login` so a fresh ID token carries `admin: true`. 5. If the UI still reports a claim refresh issue immediately after a new assignment, retry once after a short wait before treating it as a real claim-missing problem.

- 2026-04-02 | Student Google Sign-In Dead-Button Fix And Redirect Authority Cleanup

That inert path was then made more misleading by `apps/web/app/globals.css`, where disabled auth buttons kept full branded opacity and still looked active. The regular flow also did avoidable async persistence setup immediately before popup launch in `apps/web/lib/firebase/client.ts`, which increased the chance of a slow or confusing click experience.
  - What was done: Decoupled the regular Google sign-in CTA from the server-admin readiness flag, prewarmed Firebase Auth in-memory persistence through `apps/web/lib/firebase/client.ts`, added safe JSON-response guards for both bootstrap flows, added button-local busy affordances and idle guidance in `apps/web/components/auth/login-panel.tsx` and `apps/web/components/auth/admin-login-panel.tsx`, expanded user-facing auth error mapping in `apps/web/components/auth/auth-feedback.ts`, made disabled auth buttons visually disabled while keeping busy buttons visibly active in `apps/web/app/globals.css`, and made the admin bootstrap redirect server-authored by returning `redirectTo` from `apps/web/app/api/auth/admin/bootstrap/route.ts`.
  - Final redirect rules: Non-admin users remain server-authoritative through `apps/web/lib/return-to.ts`: incomplete profiles go to `/settings`, completed profiles go to `/upload`. Admins remain separated and land in `/admin`, and the admin redirect is now also server-authored instead of client-hardcoded.
  - Upload landing behavior: `/upload` remains the main post-login landing page for completed non-admin users and stays aligned with the upload-first product model. Admins intentionally remain in admin space for the cleaner security boundary.
  - Changed files:
    - `apps/web/lib/firebase/client.ts`
    - `apps/web/components/auth/auth-feedback.ts`
    - `apps/web/components/auth/login-panel.tsx`
    - `apps/web/components/auth/admin-login-panel.tsx`
    - `apps/web/app/api/auth/admin/bootstrap/route.ts`
    - `apps/web/messages/en.json`
    - `apps/web/messages/ar.json`
    - `apps/web/app/globals.css`
  - Verification: Root `npm run lint`, `npm run typecheck`, and `npm run build` all passed on 2026-04-02 after the auth fix. Live runtime checking against the existing dev server showed `/api/auth/me` reporting `runtimeFlags.firebaseAdmin: true`, and a fresh Playwright snapshot of `/login` showed the Google CTA rendered as a clickable pointer target with the new idle status copy instead of a passive dead-looking state. A full live OAuth completion test was not finished inside this environment because the sandbox/dev-server/browser setup still prevents a safe end-to-end Google popup callback run.

    - live `/login` and `/admin/login` HTML still showed the blocking missing-config banners before this repo-side fix, so the problem was real on the current rollout and not just a stale local report

    - updated `.env.example` so `NEXT_PUBLIC_FIREBASE_APP_ID` matches the active backend-linked Firebase web app `1:38079185268:web:adcd16b5e94d3d8c52ec21`

- 2026-04-02 | Canonical Firebase Deployment Model Simplification
  - What was done: Removed the root `hosting` block from `firebase.json`, kept the `apphosting`, `firestore`, and `storage` blocks intact, added explicit root deploy scripts for App Hosting and shared Firebase resources in `package.json`, and updated top-level documentation to declare Firebase App Hosting as the single canonical web deployment path for the Next.js 16 app.
  - Classic-versus-App-Hosting audit result: The conflicting classic Hosting path was being invoked by the root `hosting` block in `firebase.json`, which caused plain `firebase deploy` to include the Firebase Hosting framework-preview integration for the same `apps/web` app. The supported App Hosting path is invoked by the root `apphosting` block in `firebase.json` together with `apps/web/apphosting.yaml`.
  - Why this was necessary: Mixing Firebase Hosting's unsupported Next.js framework-preview path with Firebase App Hosting caused the repo to attempt two different deployment models for one Next.js 16 application. That created duplicate web deploy work, preview-only warnings, generated Cloud Function/framework behavior, and rollout confusion.
  - Result: The repo now has one official deployment model for the web app: Firebase App Hosting. Firestore rules/indexes and Storage rules remain deployable from the same root Firebase config, and the monorepo app root stays `apps/web`.

    - added a narrow Firestore write guard that strips only an unresolved top-level `ownerRole` field from merge writes, keeping export-artifact refreshes and other updates valid without globally enabling broad undefined-ignore behavior or guessing the wrong role
    - added best-effort read-through backfill for accessed legacy document and assessment records once the server can actually prove the owner role, so repeated preview/result/export/upload access gradually repairs old metadata instead of leaving it permanently unresolved
    - added the explicit owner-scoped migration helper `backfillLegacyOwnerRolesForOwner(ownerUid)` in `apps/web/lib/server/repository.ts` so future maintenance work can intentionally backfill whole owner histories once the authoritative role is known

    - temporary upload cleanup depended mainly on lazy access-path cleanup, which is insufficient for deterministic expiry guarantees during idle periods
  - Technical details:
    - session TTL parsing/clamping lives in `session-config.ts` (`min=60`, `default=3600`, `max=604800`) to prevent invalid env input from silently breaking auth/session behavior
    - forced/non-forced sweeps are batched (`limit=200`) and throttled (`60s`) using a runtime-global marker to avoid high-frequency repeated scans
    - maintenance authorization requires `Authorization: Bearer <ZOOTOPIA_MAINTENANCE_SECRET>` and remains server-only; if the secret is absent, the endpoint rejects requests
    - cleanup scope intentionally targets upload workspace documents only; assessment generations and retained export artifacts are left under their existing retention lifecycle
    - Firestore raw document reads now normalize missing `id` fields from document IDs so cleanup/delete operations remain stable for legacy records

    - the shared print renderer relied on content plus `margin-top: auto` footers inside static sections without a dedicated body/footer sibling structure, so dense first/support pages could consume the footer's slot and visually push the footer into the following page.
    - the support/signature/footer page was also tuned too close to the page limit after recent premium-sizing changes, leaving too little buffer for print-engine reflow.
  - What changed:

      - multiline text pressure
      - type and difficulty badges
      - choice-row overhead
      - answer/rationale card overhead
      - question-type-specific detail blocks
      - structured science blocks and their list/pair payloads
    - tightened the shared first-page and following-page complexity budgets slightly so fallback triggers earlier when rich cards would threaten the footer slot.
    - bumped `ASSESSMENT_PRINT_LAYOUT_VERSION` to `2026-04-06-compact-pdf-v23`, which also advances both Pro/Fast lane artifact versions through their existing imported version contract.
    - restructured shared print HTML so each page keeps a dedicated `page-section-body` wrapper and the footer as the final sibling row, including the Arabic support page.
    - updated static-section print CSS to reserve a small footer gutter, keep the footer in its own trailing row, and preserve the shared footer as the last element of every page section.
    - compacted the support-page print tokens slightly (padding, gaps, signature width) so the fixed support/signature/footer composition fits safely inside its page without flattening the premium visual language.
    - tuned question-card sizing carefully:
      - first-page print cards are slightly safer to protect the opening-page footer
      - following-page cards are slightly larger and a touch wider in print so later question pages fill the page better without introducing new overflow
  - What was preserved:

      - `AssessmentDailyCreditsSummary`
      - `AssessmentCreateResponse`
    - added `apps/web/lib/server/assessment-daily-credits.ts` as the server-only source of truth for:
      - the fixed daily limit (`3`)
      - the canonical UTC day window and reset timestamp
      - reservation TTL (`30 minutes`)
      - daily-ledger normalization
      - stale-reservation pruning
      - admin exemption resolution
      - UI-safe credit summaries
    - extended `apps/web/lib/server/repository.ts` with centralized assessment-credit helpers:
      - `getAssessmentDailyCreditsSummaryForUser(...)`
      - `reserveAssessmentDailyCreditAttempt(...)`
      - `releaseAssessmentDailyCreditReservation(...)`
      - `saveAssessmentGenerationWithCreditCommit(...)`
    - the repository now keeps `assessmentDailyCredits` in the in-memory fallback store for local non-Firestore runtimes and uses a dedicated Firestore collection (`assessmentDailyCredits`) when Admin SDK access is available.
    - `reserveAssessmentDailyCreditAttempt(...)` now creates a short-lived server-side reservation immediately before the model call so realistic duplicate clicks or parallel submits cannot overbook the remaining quota while generation is still in flight.
    - `saveAssessmentGenerationWithCreditCommit(...)` now binds the durable assessment save to the verified session owner UID and commits the saved generation record plus the one-success credit consumption together in the same Firestore transaction after the canonical result artifact already exists.
    - `releaseAssessmentDailyCreditReservation(...)` now runs on generation/provider/storage/finalization failures so failed attempts do not consume credits and abandoned pending slots recover automatically after cleanup or TTL expiry.
    - updated `apps/web/app/api/assessment/route.ts` so the real generation route now:
      - validates auth/profile/document ownership first
      - reserves quota only after request validation succeeds
      - keeps admin exemption on the server
      - persists the canonical result artifact before the final durable save
      - commits the saved generation plus one credit together
      - cleans up reservations on failure
      - deletes orphaned artifacts best-effort if finalization fails before a durable saved result exists
    - updated `apps/web/app/(protected)/(completed)/assessment/page.tsx` to load the current server-owned daily credit summary for the signed-in owner and pass it into the studio without moving authority client-side.
    - updated `apps/web/components/assessment/assessment-studio.tsx` so the Assessment page now shows a premium concise daily-credit panel, disables the submit button locally when the server summary is exhausted, maps the new exhausted/finalization error codes cleanly, and refreshes the displayed credit summary from the server response after each successful saved generation.

    - updated the shared protected-shell comment in `apps/web/components/layout/protected-shell.tsx` so project memory no longer incorrectly says no real credits backend exists; the shell chip still stays decorative by design.
  - Admin/user separation and session-isolation findings:
    - admin-only API handlers remain server-gated through `getAdminSessionUser()`:
      - `GET /api/admin/overview`
      - `GET /api/admin/users`
      - `PATCH /api/admin/users/[uid]/role`
      - `PATCH /api/admin/users/[uid]/status`
    - protected admin pages still resolve through `requireAdminUser()` and do not rely on hidden client UI state.
    - session identity still comes from the Firebase session cookie on every request through `verifySessionCookie(..., true)`, and suspended users are filtered server-side before a session is treated as authenticated.
    - owner-facing assessment/result/export/history reads remain bound to `ownerUid` through existing repository helpers such as `getAssessmentGenerationForOwner(...)`, so this pass did not reopen admin cross-owner access through normal user artifact routes.
    - no shared mutable in-memory session object was introduced for credits; all quota decisions are keyed from the verified request user plus a per-user per-day document.
  - Daily-credit model after this pass:
    - applies to normal users only.
    - admins are exempt.
    - the day window is fixed to UTC and resets automatically at the next UTC midnight.
    - each successful saved assessment consumes exactly one credit.
    - failed validation, missing documents, provider failures, storage failures, and durable-save failures do not consume credits.
    - the route blocks new generation attempts with `ASSESSMENT_DAILY_CREDITS_EXHAUSTED` once the daily quota is exhausted.
  - Exact decrement timing:
    - credit is not decremented on button click or at model start.
    - a short-lived reservation is taken immediately before model execution only to protect concurrency; it is not counted as usage.
    - the single credit is consumed only when the canonical result artifact already exists and the normalized assessment record is durably saved in the same final repository commit.
  - What was preserved:
    - separate regular-user and admin login/bootstrap architecture.
    - claims-first admin authority and current admin-only API/page boundaries.
    - owner-only assessment preview/result/export continuity.
    - same-origin App Router + Firebase Admin server authority.
    - Pro/Fast PDF lane separation and existing export routing.
    - current auth/session cookie architecture and self-only profile flow.
  - Honest caveat that remains:
    - the current architecture now makes the saved assessment record plus credit consumption atomic at the final Firestore step, but it still uses a temporary reservation to protect concurrency before the model runs.
    - if a process crashes after reserving a slot but before releasing or finalizing it, that slot can remain temporarily reserved until the 30-minute TTL prunes it.
    - if an in-flight generation somehow outlives that TTL and another request prunes the stale reservation first, the late generation will fail finalization safely: the result will not be kept, the credit will not be consumed, and the canonical artifact cleanup is best-effort.
    - eliminating that remaining reservation-TTL edge completely would require a larger orchestration redesign (for example a durable job/reconciliation layer), which was intentionally out of scope for this surgical pass.
  - Verification in this pass:
    - `npm run lint --workspace @zootopia/web` passed.
    - `npm run typecheck --workspace @zootopia/web` passed cleanly after the new credit/session types and route contracts were wired in.
    - `npm run build --workspace @zootopia/web` passed, and the final route tree still includes the existing admin routes, assessment result/export routes, and App Router API handlers.
    - code-level verification confirmed:
      - admin-only route enforcement still resolves through `getAdminSessionUser()` and `requireAdminUser()`.
      - direct normal-user access to admin APIs still bottoms out in server-side `FORBIDDEN`.
      - the true generation route (`POST /api/assessment`) now checks credits before model execution.
      - failed generation/provider/storage/finalization paths release the reservation and do not consume a credit.
      - successful durable saves consume exactly one credit and return the refreshed summary to the UI.
      - owner-only assessment result/export continuity still resolves through `getAssessmentGenerationForOwner(...)`.

2026-04-07 14:36:46 - Added server-side admin-auth request throttling to harden session/identifier entry points without changing session authority, route ownership, or App Hosting deployment shape.
  - Scope:
    - lightweight in-memory request rate limiting for admin auth entry routes
    - explicit 429 failure surface with Retry-After and X-RateLimit-Reset headers
    - preserved existing admin claim, allowlist, and recent-sign-in validation chain
  - Files changed in this pass:
    - apps/web/lib/server/request-rate-limit.ts (new)
    - apps/web/app/api/auth/admin/resolve-identifier/route.ts
    - apps/web/app/api/auth/admin/bootstrap/route.ts
    - zootopia-club-next-ledger.txt
  - Why this was required:
    - admin auth routes accepted unlimited repeated attempts per client fingerprint, leaving unnecessary brute-force and enumeration pressure even though session and claim checks were already server-authoritative.
  - Implementation details:
    - introduced checkRequestRateLimit(...) in apps/web/lib/server/request-rate-limit.ts using a process-local global map keyed by route scope plus client fingerprint (forwarded IP + user agent).
    - added pruning guard for expired windows to keep memory bounded in long-lived runtime processes.
    - applied guard to /api/auth/admin/resolve-identifier at 20 requests per 60 seconds per fingerprint.
    - applied guard to /api/auth/admin/bootstrap at 10 requests per 60 seconds per fingerprint.
    - blocked responses return AUTH_RATE_LIMITED with 429, Retry-After, and X-RateLimit-Reset for predictable client retry behavior.
    - architecture-sensitive note: this is intentionally a minimal in-memory gate suitable for current server-authoritative same-origin deployment; if global cross-instance limits become necessary later, this helper is the narrow replacement point for managed shared-rate infrastructure.
  - What was preserved:
    - Firebase Admin verification flow, session cookie minting, admin allowlist checks, and claim activation path are unchanged.
    - route contracts and ownership boundaries were preserved; no browser authority was introduced.
    - no new npm dependencies were added.
  - Verification in this pass:
    - npm run lint --workspace @zootopia/web passed.
    - npm run typecheck --workspace @zootopia/web passed.
    - npm run build --workspace @zootopia/web passed.
    - build output still includes /api/auth/admin/bootstrap and /api/auth/admin/resolve-identifier.

- 2026-04-08 23:58:00 | Settings Phone Verification Render-Loop Stabilization + OTP/Admin Runtime QA
  - Mandatory-first-step compliance:
    - reread `zootopia-club-next-ledger.txt` fully before implementation.
    - executed required parallel read-only subagent exploration first (architecture/dependencies, Settings form-state tracing, phone/OTP runtime tracing, server validation/session/profile-completion tracing, and verification strategy), then validated all target files directly before editing.
  - Problem observed in this pass:
    - typing in the Settings phone number field could trigger React runtime churn ending in `Maximum update depth exceeded`.
    - risk source was a controlled-value feedback cycle between `react-phone-number-input` intermediate emissions and repeated state writes inside the local phone draft updater.
  - Root-cause notes:
    - `react-phone-number-input` can emit both E.164-like and country-scoped intermediate values while users edit.
    - pre-normalizing at the input edge plus re-normalizing in updater paths allowed repeated writes that resolved to the same effective phone state, causing avoidable rerender loops under specific edit/caret sequences.
  - What changed (surgical, backward-compatible):
    - `apps/web/components/settings/profile-settings-form.tsx`
      - updated `normalizePhoneDraftValue(...)` to accept optional fallback country calling code and canonicalize both international and national intermediate values into one stable `+<digits>` draft.
      - updated `updatePhoneDraft(...)` to normalize with the resolved country calling code and bail out early when both country + normalized number are unchanged.
      - updated `PhoneNumberInput` `onChange` to pass the raw library value (`nextValue ?? ""`) directly to `updatePhoneDraft(...)` so normalization ownership is centralized in one place.
      - strengthened OTP code input semantics for reliability/accessibility (`id`, `name`, `maxLength=6`) while preserving existing flow/labels/actions.
      - added high-value comments documenting loop-prevention rationale and verification-state invalidation intent.
    - runtime QA scripts added for this pass:
      - `.tmp/settings-phone-loop-qa.mjs` (typed-input loop detection + send-code interaction diagnostics)
      - `.tmp/settings-admin-smoke.mjs` (admin Settings page smoke check)
  - Architecture/runtime ownership preserved intentionally:
    - Firebase client phone auth flow remains unchanged (`RecaptchaVerifier` + `signInWithPhoneNumber`).
    - server-authoritative verification persistence remains unchanged (`/api/users/me/phone-verification`).
    - profile-completion server recomputation and admin exemption paths remain unchanged.
    - no secret handling/client authority changes introduced.
  - Path analysis status (requested scopes):
    - local integrated runtime (`apps/web` app + API, same-origin): validated via health + authenticated runtime QA.
