- 2026-04-09 00:32:15 | Settings Phone Render-Loop Guard Refinement (Deep Normalization Mismatch Fix)
  - Mandatory-first-step compliance:
    - reread `zootopia-club-next-ledger.txt` fully before implementation.
    - executed a read-only Explore subagent sweep first to diagnose the exact root cause before any code changes.
    - checked local Next.js docs for App Router and client-side patterns.
  - Runtime issue diagnosed:
    - upon typing into the Settings phone field, `Maximum update depth exceeded` error at line 1044 (PhoneNumberInput component).
    - subagent root-cause analysis revealed the guard at line 500 was failing because it compared two differently-normalized values.
  - Exact root cause:
    - Line 500 comparison: `const phoneChanged = normalizedPhoneValue !== normalizedNextPhoneValue;`
    - `normalizedPhoneValue` comes from `normalizePhoneForCompare()` (simple trim + whitespace removal)
    - `normalizedNextPhoneValue` comes from `normalizePhoneDraftValue()` (full phone normalization + digit-capping)
    - These two functions produce different string representations for the same phone value.

- 2026-04-09 13:27:04 | Firebase App Hosting Deploy Fix (EntityTooLarge Source Upload)
  - Mandatory-first-step compliance:
    - reread `zootopia-club-next-ledger.txt` before implementation.
    - reproduced the deployment failure with `--debug` to confirm exact backend error before editing config.
    - consulted Firebase workflow guidance skill for CLI/auth/project checks.
  - Issue observed:
    - `firebase deploy` failed during App Hosting source upload with:
      - `Unable to parse JSON: Unexpected token '<' ...`
    - debug logs confirmed the underlying error was not JSON parsing of local config, but Cloud Storage upload rejection:
      - `Code>EntityTooLarge</Code>`
      - `Content-length exceeds upper bound on range`
  - Root cause:
    - App Hosting source archive was including large local artifacts from `apps/web` (notably build/output history artifacts), causing upload size to exceed the policy limit for source uploads.
  - What changed (surgical):
    - `firebase.json`
      - extended `apphosting.ignore` to exclude heavy non-source artifacts from upload:
        - `.next`
        - `output`
        - `.history`
        - `.tmp`
        - `tsconfig.tsbuildinfo`
      - existing ignore entries (`node_modules`, `.git`, firebase debug logs, `functions`) were preserved.
  - What was preserved intentionally:
    - no runtime architecture changes.
    - no apphosting backend id/rootDir changes.
    - no env/secret contract changes in `apps/web/apphosting.yaml`.
    - no app code or API route behavior changes.
  - Verification in this pass:
    - `firebase.json` parsed successfully after edit.
    - reran deployment with debug:
      - `npx -y firebase-tools@latest deploy --only apphosting:zootopia-club-next-backend --debug`
      - result: rollout completed successfully with exit code 0.
      - terminal ended with:
        - `+  apphosting: Rollout for backend zootopia-club-next-backend complete!`
        - `+  Deploy complete!`
    - When `react-phone-number-input` fires onChange with its internal normalization, our comparison always finds a difference (even when there isn't one semantically).
    - The guard fails to prevent no-op state updates → `setPhoneValue()` called → new render → different `normalizedPhoneValue` prop → `PhoneNumberInput` fires onChange again → infinite loop escalates.
  - What changed:
    - `apps/web/components/settings/profile-settings-form.tsx` (line 500)
      - changed guard comparison from: `const phoneChanged = normalizedPhoneValue !== normalizedNextPhoneValue;`
      - to: `const phoneChanged = phoneValue !== normalizedNextPhoneValue;`
      - rationale: `phoneValue` is the actual state we're about to update to, so comparing it against `normalizedNextPhoneValue` ensures both sides use consistent normalization (the value that will be set is the value to compare against).
      - updated comment to clarify why the comparison uses the state value rather than a derived memoized value.
  - What was preserved intentionally:
    - Firebase OTP flow remains unchanged.
    - all server contracts and auth authority unchanged.
    - no design, dependency, or unrelated settings logic touched.
    - no removal of previous fixes or prior guard logic—this is a refinement of the existing guard.
  - Verification in this pass:
    - `npm run lint --workspace @zootopia/web` passed.
    - `npm run typecheck --workspace @zootopia/web` passed.
    - `npm run build --workspace @zootopia/web` passed.
  - Files changed in this pass:
    - `apps/web/components/settings/profile-settings-form.tsx`
    - `zootopia-club-next-ledger.txt`
